# user (default) (TextMessage): 

<blueprint>
Final position adjustment notes
- Moved wheels to y=±4 to clear cannons.
- Re-anchored winches to TOP faces of deck gussets.
- Transverse ties now use BOTTOM faces of gussets across the deck.
- Under-deck fan rewired to bottom nodes; added tabs 300–301 to avoid face congestion.
- Decorative buttresses use TOP faces of finials and TOP faces of top gussets.
- Torches set to 12° outward tilt to meet ≥0.35 wood-clearance.

# builder (gpt-5) (ThoughtEvent): 

Welcome to the build session. Here are the tools I will use in this 3D simulated environment, how they help, and what information I need from each instruction:

- functions.start
  - What it does: Creates the very first (root) block of the machine at a specified position and rotation.
  - What I need: init_shift [x, y, z], init_rotation [yaw, pitch, roll] if any, and a descriptive note about what the machine/block represents.
  - Why note matters: The note is a powerful identifier that documents the purpose of this starting block (e.g., “Block 1 – base at deck center”), making later references unambiguous.

- functions.attach_block_to
  - What it does: Attaches a new block to a specific face of an existing block. Supported new block types: Small Wooden Block, Powered Wheel, Torch, Water Cannon.
  - What I need: base_block ID, the face of the base block to attach to (faces are labeled with capitalized directions like NORTH, SOUTH, EAST, WEST, TOP, BOTTOM; I can verify using get_block_details if needed), the type of new block, and a clear note describing the function (e.g., “Block 3 – East deck at y=+1”).
  - Why note matters: Notes will carry the blueprint’s identifiers and roles so we can reliably track every element.

- functions.connect_blocks
  - What it does: Connects two existing blocks using a connector: Brace or Winch.
  - What I need: IDs of both blocks, the exact faces to connect from/to (again, using correct face names; I can query with get_block_details), the connector type, and a descriptive note (e.g., “X lattice k=0 ascending”).
  - Constraints: Connection fails if faces are too close; if necessary, we may adjust positions via shift_block first.
  - Why note matters: Notes identify each structural tie, cable, or brace so we can audit the lattice later.

- functions.shift_block
  - What it does: Applies a small positional offset to a block after attachment ([x, y, z] each in −0.5…+0.5). Useful if an attachment fails due to overlap.
  - What I need: block_id and shift vector.
  - Caution: Excessive shift may detach the block; I will use small corrections only and document them.

- functions.twist_block
  - What it does: Rotates a block clockwise about its rooted surface by a specified angle (degrees). Particularly for directional or pointer-like blocks.
  - What I need: block_id and angle in degrees. I can apply multiple twists to achieve the exact direction.
  - Use case: Setting torch tilt (e.g., 12° outward) when geometry requires orientation adjustments.

- functions.flip_spin
  - What it does: Flips the spin direction on spinning blocks (e.g., Powered Wheels) if they have an active spin.
  - What I need: block_id. Only applicable if the block spins; if ornamental with auto-brake, we likely won’t need it, but it’s available.

- functions.get_block_details
  - What it does: Retrieves full details for a specific block including face labels and orientation.
  - What I need: block_id. I’ll use this to confirm exact face names (NORTH, SOUTH, EAST, WEST, TOP, BOTTOM) before making complex connections or when “outward face” needs clarification.

- functions.get_machine_summary
  - What it does: Returns the latest state overview of the machine. This is a mandatory final check before ending a build session to ensure consistency.
  - Important: I will remind you and perform this check before we finish the process.

- functions.remove_block
  - What it does: Removes a block by ID if a correction is needed.
  - What I need: block_id. I’ll reattach with the correct parameters and note.

- functions.reset
  - What it does: Clears the entire machine to the initial empty state if we must start over.

Notes are crucial across all tools—they serve as human-readable IDs and functions for each block (e.g., “Deck gusset y=+2 east outward”), enabling precise verification against your blueprint and quick troubleshooting.

Build plan based on your blueprint
- I will follow your final blueprint strictly, one block or connection at a time, in numerical order.
- I will attach Small Wooden Blocks to build the deck slab and piers first, then posts, finials, gussets/tabs, bottom nodes, torch tabs, lattice braces, transverse ties, under-deck fan truss elements, winches (suspension cables), powered wheels, water cannons, torches, and final decorative buttresses.
- When face ambiguity might arise (e.g., “outward face”), I’ll use get_block_details to confirm orientations.
- Before we conclude, I will run get_machine_summary for a final audit (mandatory).
- Motion/control settings you specified (e.g., powered wheels unactuated, cannons off) will be respected.
